  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8493e3c5-a341-495d-bda5-1b9b646f0fff'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2834433210518380757">The body is where our instincts reside and where we fight, flee, or freeze, and it endures the trauma inflicted by the ills that plague society. In this groundbreaking work, therapist Resmaa Menakem examines the damage caused by racism in America from the perspective of body-centered psychology. He argues this destruction will continue until Americans learn to heal the gen</span>
  <span id="freeText2834433210518380757" style="display:none">The body is where our instincts reside and where we fight, flee, or freeze, and it endures the trauma inflicted by the ills that plague society. In this groundbreaking work, therapist Resmaa Menakem examines the damage caused by racism in America from the perspective of body-centered psychology. He argues this destruction will continue until Americans learn to heal the generational anguish of white supremacy, which is deeply embedded in all our bodies. Our collective agony doesn't just affect African Americans. White Americans suffer their own secondary trauma as well. So do blue Americans—our police.<br /><br /><i>My Grandmother's Hands</i> is a call to action for all of us to recognize that racism is not about the head, but about the body, and introduces an alternative view of what we can do to grow beyond our entrenched racialized divide.<br /><br /><br /><br />Paves the way for a new, body-centered understanding of white supremacy—how it is literally in our blood and our nervous system.<br /><br /><br />Offers a step-by-step solution—a healing process—in addition to incisive social commentary.<br /><br /><b>Resmaa Menakem, MSW, LICSW</b>, is a therapist with decades of experience currently in private practice in Minneapolis, MN, specializing in trauma, body-centered psychotherapy, and violence prevention. He has appeared on the <i>Oprah Winfrey Show</i> and <i>Dr. Phil</i> as an expert on conflict and violence. Menakem has studied with bestselling authors Dr. David Schnarch (<i>Passionate Marriage</i>) and Dr. Bessel van der Kolk (<i>The Body Keeps the Score</i>). He also trained at Peter Levine's Somatic Experiencing Trauma Institute.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2834433210518380757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_2890041038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2890041038" />
    <a title="Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61877628-lawrence"><img alt="Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550492234p2/61877628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2890041038?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lawrence" href="/user/show/61877628-lawrence">Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61877628-lawrence?shelf=all-black-everything">all-black-everything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61877628-lawrence?shelf=healing">healing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61877628-lawrence?shelf=somatics">somatics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61877628-lawrence?shelf=movement">movement</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61877628-lawrence?shelf=race">race</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2890041038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14341149029035928298">**What are the main ideas?** <br/><br/>* white supremacy is more accurately called white-body supremacy. it's got less to do with supremacy of white skin and more to do with supremacy of bodies that are considered white. this could be seen as semantic but is quite helpful. <br/>* white-body supremacy lives in our BODIES; it's in our blood, dna, flesh, and the pre-cognitive parts of our brains (aka the lizard brain).<br/>* as such, trainings that focus on the mind as the site from which to undo white-body supremacy </span>
  <span id="freeText14341149029035928298" style="display:none">**What are the main ideas?** <br /><br />* white supremacy is more accurately called white-body supremacy. it's got less to do with supremacy of white skin and more to do with supremacy of bodies that are considered white. this could be seen as semantic but is quite helpful. <br />* white-body supremacy lives in our BODIES; it's in our blood, dna, flesh, and the pre-cognitive parts of our brains (aka the lizard brain).<br />* as such, trainings that focus on the mind as the site from which to undo white-body supremacy will never be enough. <br />* undoing white-body supremacy is first and foremost a somatic endeavor. the cognitive/thinking parts will flow second (because the lizard brain, the part tied to our vegus nerve, is both faster than cognition AND the vegus nerve can override cognition). <br />* clean pain is when you know that a difficult thing needs to be done, you know what that thing is, and you do it because healing/growth are on the other side. dirty pain is all the subsequent pain when clean pain is avoided. <br />* a settled body accepts attempts at healing (clean pain). an unsettled body rejects attempts at healing (and therefore creates dirty pain). <br />* settling your body is not the same as healing, but you will improve your capacity to heal when you can settle your body. <br />* the trauma of american slavery is rooted in the trauma of european bodies through the middle ages. whipping and hangings started in europe because they were brought to the u.s. the people who brought slaves to the u.s. need to heal their ancestral trauma in order for folks on this soil to move forward.<br /><br /><br />**If I implemented one idea from this book right now, which one would it be?**<br /><br />* anti-racism work is somatic. we need to create opportunities for people's actual bodies to learn how to have non-traumatic responses to bodies that they have lizard brain reactions to. those reactions that are based in trauma, are not helpful because they are knee-jerk and not intentional or conscious. <br /><br />**How would I describe the book to a friend?**<br /><br />this is a theoretical guide book and instruction manual for how to actually undo white(-body) supremacy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14341149029035928298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Erika Sanders" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64198312-erika-sanders"><img alt="Erika Sanders" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487174538p2/64198312.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2206716021?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erika Sanders" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erika Sanders" href="/user/show/64198312-erika-sanders">Erika Sanders</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2206716021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8715467460576153836">I've studied racism and been part of anti-racism work for over 25 years, and I have to say, this book is one of the most valuable pieces of work on the topic that I've read. Menakem's teachings don't replace or supplant other racial liberation tactics or philosophies, but instead give us a fresh way to expand how we understand the lived racial experience we ALL have. It gives us another road into this work, a road that seems essential to travel, even as we commit and recommit ourselves to multip</span>
  <span id="freeText8715467460576153836" style="display:none">I've studied racism and been part of anti-racism work for over 25 years, and I have to say, this book is one of the most valuable pieces of work on the topic that I've read. Menakem's teachings don't replace or supplant other racial liberation tactics or philosophies, but instead give us a fresh way to expand how we understand the lived racial experience we ALL have. It gives us another road into this work, a road that seems essential to travel, even as we commit and recommit ourselves to multiple additional types of racial liberation work. Plus, Menakem's writing style is accessible, clear and blunt - just what this topic needs.<br /><br />It feels hokey and overblown to say, but I'll say it anyway - this should be on the reading list of anyone and everyone who cares about racial justice and liberation in the US.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8715467460576153836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3151554387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3151554387" />
    <a title="Leila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11317222-leila"><img alt="Leila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579976560p2/11317222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3151554387?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leila" href="/user/show/11317222-leila">Leila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11317222-leila?shelf=2020-books-by-poc">2020-books-by-poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11317222-leila?shelf=trauma-and-healing">trauma-and-healing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3151554387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15620418160996444304">2.5 stars<br/><br/>I had been so excited to finally find a book about trauma that talked about the ways that racism and systemic oppression inflict trauma, and this book was a starting point but not fully there. If you can get past the cop apologia (his brother is a cop, and he trains police departments), the offensive language (e.g. “yellow bodies” and “red bodies”), some fatphobia, and the whole concept of “police bodies,” there are some gems in here — particularly in part 2. There are specific breathin</span>
  <span id="freeText15620418160996444304" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />I had been so excited to finally find a book about trauma that talked about the ways that racism and systemic oppression inflict trauma, and this book was a starting point but not fully there. If you can get past the cop apologia (his brother is a cop, and he trains police departments), the offensive language (e.g. “yellow bodies” and “red bodies”), some fatphobia, and the whole concept of “police bodies,” there are some gems in here — particularly in part 2. There are specific breathing exercises and strategies to help settle your body and, as Menakem writes, act "from the best parts of yourself." I also really appreciated the ideas about how to better protect ourselves from internalizing oppression, not just on a cognitive level but on a somatic level. That said, the ways that Menakem has seemingly internalized oppressive ideas about weight, for example, shows us that we need BOTH cognitive and somatic approaches. For prison and police abolitionists, I recommend skipping the chapters on police entirely, as Menakem seems to believe that cops just need to be trained to heal their trauma in order to end police violence. 🙃 It felt particularly strange to me that he was able to trace the history of white people's violence, but when it came to policing, he made it seem as though policing in the U.S. was once useful for protecting communities and somehow lost its way, which seemed ahistorical. The first two chapters of part 3 are very good, but the rest of the chapters in that section are redundant. I think I would’ve given the book 4 stars if I had known in advance to skip the harmful and redundant chapters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15620418160996444304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12206425456501149950">"A calm, settled body is the foundation for health, for healing, for helping others, and for changing the world."<br/><br/>I’ve been reading this book s-l-o-w-l-y because the author wants the reader to stop and actually do the practices. There is a lot here about dealing with racialized trauma, not only for individuals but within communities. Specific practices are for black people, and others for white people.   <span id="freeText12206425456501149950" style="display:none">"A calm, settled body is the foundation for health, for healing, for helping others, and for changing the world."<br /><br />I’ve been reading this book s-l-o-w-l-y because the author wants the reader to stop and actually do the practices. There is a lot here about dealing with racialized trauma, not only for individuals but within communities. Specific practices are for black people, and others for white people. There are several chapters about rethinking how police are trained to deal with trauma as well.<br /><br />If you know mindfulness practices, some of the practices here will be familiar if not quite the same. The strategies for settling the body are definitely some I will be working with.<br /><br />He ends the book with a challenge for transforming communities and everyday activism. I read this in Hoopla but need to buy it as it isn’t possible to absorb it all the first time.</span>

<div id="review_2254883459" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2254883459" />
    <a title="cat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77925-cat"><img alt="cat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208438341p2/77925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2254883459?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="cat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="cat" href="/user/show/77925-cat">cat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77925-cat?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2254883459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5853423763987466924">I don't even know where to start with a review of this book. It is such a powerful addition to the conversation about trauma, about white supremacy, about bodily healing of trauma -- and specifically the way that bodies hold the trauma of white body supremacy. The trauma is not only held by bodies of color, and this author actually addresses bodies of color, white bodies, and law enforcement bodies each individually, as well as collective/communal healing of all bodies. There is a lot of unpacki</span>
  <span id="freeText5853423763987466924" style="display:none">I don't even know where to start with a review of this book. It is such a powerful addition to the conversation about trauma, about white supremacy, about bodily healing of trauma -- and specifically the way that bodies hold the trauma of white body supremacy. The trauma is not only held by bodies of color, and this author actually addresses bodies of color, white bodies, and law enforcement bodies each individually, as well as collective/communal healing of all bodies. There is a lot of unpacking of what types of somatic healing are necessary to help bring about an end to racial violence -- and the ways that we can engage in that work individually and with groups of trusted comrades. Menakem uses a synopsis feature at the end of each chapter that has been so helpful to me as I have gone back and forth between chapters, re-engaging with ideas shared previously, and also has body/breath practice activities throughout the chapters that I found so valuable. <br /><br />There is way more to be said about this book -- and I may return to say some of it later. Until then, this book ranks up there with Bessel Van Der Kolk's 'The Body Keeps the Score' in terms of resources for considering the healing required for trauma -- racial, sexual, war-related, intergenerational, and even genetically coded. All trauma requires healing that uses mind, body, and soul. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5853423763987466924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2186886119" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2186886119" />
    <a title="Novel Addiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73909712-novel-addiction"><img alt="Novel Addiction" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/images/nophoto/user/c_111x148.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2186886119?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Novel Addiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Novel Addiction" href="/user/show/73909712-novel-addiction">Novel Addiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2186886119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4114654868760832142">What impressed me most about 'My Grandmother's Hands', was how well author Resmaa Menakem tackled the controversial topic that is racism. He was made no accusations, and doesn't lecture the reader. He isn't saying that all white people are racist or all black people are distrustful. What he suggests – rather convincingly – is that racial prejudice can be carried within our bodies, caused by the traumatic experiences of those that came before us. I loved how personal and insightful this book was,</span>
  <span id="freeText4114654868760832142" style="display:none">What impressed me most about 'My Grandmother's Hands', was how well author Resmaa Menakem tackled the controversial topic that is racism. He was made no accusations, and doesn't lecture the reader. He isn't saying that all white people are racist or all black people are distrustful. What he suggests – rather convincingly – is that racial prejudice can be carried within our bodies, caused by the traumatic experiences of those that came before us. I loved how personal and insightful this book was, it has the capacity to change a lot of lives. The experiences of the generations before us, may have marked our souls, but we don't have to pass that mark onto the next generation. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4114654868760832142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3527781114" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3527781114" />
    <a title="Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72793544-tichana-the-book-hobbit"><img alt="Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598682051p2/72793544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3527781114?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) " href="/user/show/72793544-tichana-the-book-hobbit">Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72793544-tichana-the-book-hobbit?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72793544-tichana-the-book-hobbit?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3527781114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3395491673654962697"><b> **** 2.25 Stars **** </b> <br/><br/><i> My Grandmother's Hands </i> was an interesting book about racialized trauma and its effects on our bodies. <br/>While the concept of the book sounds brilliant, I was a bit disappointed with its content. <br/>-The book is divided in 3 parts. The first part is pretty much Resmaa Menakem stating the same thing over and over and preparing the reader for what his book is going to be about. I found this to be unnecessary and a waste of time. I just wanted him to get to the point. There was n</span>
  <span id="freeText3395491673654962697" style="display:none"><b> **** 2.25 Stars **** </b> <br /><br /><i> My Grandmother's Hands </i> was an interesting book about racialized trauma and its effects on our bodies. <br />While the concept of the book sounds brilliant, I was a bit disappointed with its content. <br />-The book is divided in 3 parts. The first part is pretty much Resmaa Menakem stating the same thing over and over and preparing the reader for what his book is going to be about. I found this to be unnecessary and a waste of time. I just wanted him to get to the point. There was no need for him to mention multiple times what books he wrote, what TV shows he's been on, or how his brother is a police officer. It was extremely redundant. <br />-Once you get past part 1, the book becomes interesting. It talks about how racialized trauma can pass from one generation to another and how we are all victims of it and we need to heal in order to move forward. The books also touches on police brutality in the US and how it can improve. I did not agree with this part in particular because it implied that the policing system is a good system found on good intentions and that once it heals, it will get better. I think the problem of police brutality in the US is much bigger than that. <br />-The book also has useful breathing exercises and other strategies to help cope with trauma and heal it. <br />-I found Menakem's use of language to be offensive sometimes. For example, he continuously refers to indigenous people as "red bodies" and Asian people as "yellow bodies" which I think is ignorant and reinforces a stereotype. I found it inappropriate in a book that deals with racialized trauma and systematic racism in general. <br />-I also noticed stereotypical ideas about weight and overweight people. I did not appreciate that and I do not think it was necessary at all.<br /><br />I think I expected a lot more from this book and I went into it with high expectations. But once I started reading it, I was disappointed. The book is not bad, but it is not great either. It has some useful information on racialized trauma and healing and the exercises provided are really useful. But it had many flaws and I couldn't get past them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3395491673654962697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3438926644" />
    <a title="Dominic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2551271-dominic"><img alt="Dominic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578105289p2/2551271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3438926644?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dominic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dominic" href="/user/show/2551271-dominic">Dominic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551271-dominic?shelf=nonfic">nonfic</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3438926644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2553519770497013014">How are you still doing the work of dismantling racism?<br/>.<br/>My summer of learning comes to a close, and on Monday, I begin a school year marked by remote teaching. So I couldn't be happier with my last book of the summer. Since this book is on backorder just about everywhere, I had to settle for the audiobook.<br/><br/>Ever since hearing Resmaa Menakem in conversation with Krista Tippett for her *on being* podcast (twice!), I knew I had to read this book. Menakem proposes that we'll not achieve racial healing</span>
  <span id="freeText2553519770497013014" style="display:none">How are you still doing the work of dismantling racism?<br />.<br />My summer of learning comes to a close, and on Monday, I begin a school year marked by remote teaching. So I couldn't be happier with my last book of the summer. Since this book is on backorder just about everywhere, I had to settle for the audiobook.<br /><br />Ever since hearing Resmaa Menakem in conversation with Krista Tippett for her *on being* podcast (twice!), I knew I had to read this book. Menakem proposes that we'll not achieve racial healing and cultural change with solely cognitive understandings or political/activist strategy. It is through achieving a "settling" within our bodies that we can personally and collectively heal/break the cycle of generational trauma. And this has SO MANY implications for teaching; teachers CAN be healers and CAN create classroom culture that is safe, healthy, and inclusive.<br /><br />I've spent my entire life trying to feel comfortable in my body, and I'm still getting there. Fiction books about trauma often get under my skin (in the best possible way)and can be like a balm when couched with depictions of love and healthy relationships. What Menakem offers here that works so well in conjunction with that literature is a reminder that we are bodies as well as minds, *even when we read.* And in most situations, we are bodies first.<br /><br />On Monday I meet my students virtually. But I plan to integrate meditation and mindfulness and some of Menakem's breathing techniques every week--poetry one day, mindfulness the other. If you are able to get your hands on a physical copy of this book, you are in luck! I recommend the print version for all the mindfulness exercises, which I'm bound to return to often. The audiobook was still pretty great and you get instant access, and this is urgent content.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2553519770497013014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2420196437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420196437" />
    <a title="Anne Phyfe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37153025-anne-phyfe"><img alt="Anne Phyfe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439775526p2/37153025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2420196437?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Phyfe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Phyfe" href="/user/show/37153025-anne-phyfe">Anne Phyfe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420196437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13559565805746716402">Trauma is held in the body. And many (including me) believe that all Americans carry in our bodies the incredible trauma of the past four hundred years of American history, whether unconsciously or not. In this generous book, Resmaa Menakem, MSW, gives reader a context for this trauma, and a pathway to mend it, through the body. His background as a practitioner trained in Somatic Experiencing offers a rich layering of understanding that I found immediately helpful. <br/>I learned a great deal from th</span>
  <span id="freeText13559565805746716402" style="display:none">Trauma is held in the body. And many (including me) believe that all Americans carry in our bodies the incredible trauma of the past four hundred years of American history, whether unconsciously or not. In this generous book, Resmaa Menakem, MSW, gives reader a context for this trauma, and a pathway to mend it, through the body. His background as a practitioner trained in Somatic Experiencing offers a rich layering of understanding that I found immediately helpful. <br />I learned a great deal from this book, especially from the practices you are required to do before continuing. In one practice, you simply imagine someone sitting across from you with their arms crossed in front of their body, a scowl on their face. I sat in bed, reading, totally relaxed, and consciously safe. As I visualized this person, I felt as if worms were literally crawling up by shoulders and neck. The creep of tension was completely out of my control. I was left with more of a visceral awareness of my autonomic nervous system and curious about the constant tension in bodies that are perpetually watched, and on the watch, blamed, and blaming, hated, and hating. <br />I strongly recommend this book, and would love to have a discussion with anyone else who wants to talk.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13559565805746716402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2854154818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2854154818" />
    <a title="C.E. G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1831532-c-e-g"><img alt="C.E. G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1260155448p2/1831532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2854154818?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.E. G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.E. G" href="/user/show/1831532-c-e-g">C.E. G</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1831532-c-e-g?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1831532-c-e-g?shelf=race-racism">race-racism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2854154818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16300143295008700069">This adds such an important somatic lens for anti-racist conversations and work. I highly recommend this book for white people, as the exercises and suggestions helped me feel out the white supremacy my body holds and figure out regular practices that can help weaken or release it. <br/><br/>However, this book only covers anti-Black racism coming from white people and police officers. Anti-indigenous racism is such a central experience for white people in America, it feels incomplete to not address its ro</span>
  <span id="freeText16300143295008700069" style="display:none">This adds such an important somatic lens for anti-racist conversations and work. I highly recommend this book for white people, as the exercises and suggestions helped me feel out the white supremacy my body holds and figure out regular practices that can help weaken or release it. <br /><br />However, this book only covers anti-Black racism coming from white people and police officers. Anti-indigenous racism is such a central experience for white people in America, it feels incomplete to not address its role in white body supremacy, but since the author is Black, it makes sense that he's speaking to what he knows (though it would have been that much more powerful to co-author with an Indigenous person). And while the book has chapters for Black readers, non-Black POC aren't addressed in this book.<br /><br />Resmaa Menakem is also pretty tight with police in his life, with his brother being an officer and a lot of his own work being with the Minneapolis Police Department. While I sympathize that police officers are also human beings and it's essential that someone does the work of making them less harmful, I'm not as hopeful as the author that the institution of policing can be reformed. One of his tips was to smile and greet police officers at protests and marches, with the reasoning that they'll be less likely to brutalize protesters if we can calm their nervous systems through these interactions. I see that logic, but I also think it's complicated for white people to do that at BLM actions.<br /><br />There were definitely some other suggestions that I found a little odd - like white people renaming themselves after civil rights figures as a way of committing to a healthier white identity. I think if a white person I knew renamed themselves Rosa Parks Smith, I would find it off-putting and performative. <br /><br />But overall, despite our political (and perhaps generational?) differences, I still recommend that white people in particular read this, as I haven't read anything else that looks at whiteness in quite this way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16300143295008700069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8272700059710212883" style="display:none">While I have to admit that I did not do any of the body exercises, I absolutely loved this book. <div id="review_2488084996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2488084996" />
    <a title="A. Breeze Harper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1534493-a-breeze-harper"><img alt="A. Breeze Harper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413570114p2/1534493.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2488084996?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A. Breeze Harper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A. Breeze Harper" href="/user/show/1534493-a-breeze-harper">A. Breeze Harper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36167466-my-grandmother-s-hands">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2488084996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2820155613438978335"><strong>Excellent trauma-informed analysis of antiBlack racism & healing</strong><br/><br/>This book was a great and informative read. I appreciated the approach of using trauma-informed practices to understand how racial healing is most likely only possible once everyone engages in the process of “clean pain” vs. “dirty pain.” </span>

<div id="review_3226430216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3226430216" />
    <a title="Liz Castle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34494273-liz-castle"><img alt="Liz Castle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603070973p2/34494273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3226430216?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Castle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Castle" href="/user/show/34494273-liz-castle">Liz Castle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3226430216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6824578250123769660">Life changing read, as a white reader (author mostly addresses white and black readers). Several mind-blowing moments, especially the theory that white Americans still carry intergenerational trauma from the Middle Ages in Europe, and that this unhealed trauma fuels racism in America. The root of that trauma is a deep fear of powerful white people, and healing that fear is a necessary step towards liberation for us all. There are body healing practices sprinkled throughout the book that are usef</span>
  <span id="freeText6824578250123769660" style="display:none">Life changing read, as a white reader (author mostly addresses white and black readers). Several mind-blowing moments, especially the theory that white Americans still carry intergenerational trauma from the Middle Ages in Europe, and that this unhealed trauma fuels racism in America. The root of that trauma is a deep fear of powerful white people, and healing that fear is a necessary step towards liberation for us all. There are body healing practices sprinkled throughout the book that are useful tools to continue healing work. <br /><br />Highly recommend to white readers, especially white liberals. Racism lives in our bodies and we need to heal (in addition to organize, support PoC, etc.) to stop passing embodied racism (our intergenerational trauma) from generation to generation. Can’t speak to the sections on black trauma healing, but am interested to hear more on black readers’ thoughts. <br /><br />Would rate 5 stars, but was disappointed to encounter chapters on police reform through trauma therapy. There’s no doubt that cops need trauma therapy and that it would result in less violence, but the author does not mention prison abolition and the eradication of our criminal justice system altogether as being necessary to fight racism. if you don’t have the interest/energy in considering police trauma, i recommend skipping those chapters altogether. Also, the author focuses almost entirely on black folks and white folks, so I’m guessing this book would not be as useful for readers who don’t fit into either category. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6824578250123769660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7132783897168479854"><br/>I received a copy of this book, free, through Goodread Giveaways.<br/><br/>There is a growing bulk of indications that we hold trauma not only in our brains, our emotions, but it is carried generationally in our bodies. <br/><br/>“Contrary to what many people believe, trauma is not primarily an emotion response.   <span id="freeText7132783897168479854" style="display:none"><br />I received a copy of this book, free, through Goodread Giveaways.<br /><br />There is a growing bulk of indications that we hold trauma not only in our brains, our emotions, but it is carried generationally in our bodies. <br /><br />“Contrary to what many people believe, trauma is not primarily an emotion response. Trauma always happens in the body. It is a spontaneous protective mechanism used by the body to stop or thwart further (or future) potential damage. (p 7)<br /><br />This carefully written and sensitive book explores this around the trauma of race in our culture and offers a wide variety of understanding and possible activities to reclaim a wholeness for both people of color and people of European descent with some particular activities directed toward law enforcement.<br /><br />“You have the power to stop intergenerational and historical trauma in its tracks, and to keep it from spreading from your body to others. Above all, you have the power to hear. But first you have to choose to heal.” (p 212)<br /><br />While I cannot speak directly to the efficacy of the techniques offered, the book offers it ideas gently and with some wonderful quotes—both current and historic. It was a most interesting read.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3460854942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3460854942" />
    <a title="Apollo Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64019035-apollo-grace"><img alt="Apollo Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486640508p2/64019035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3460854942?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apollo Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apollo Grace" href="/user/show/64019035-apollo-grace">Apollo Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3460854942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4717580172048387657">This is a wonderful book. It gave me a rich new way to understand and think about how racism operates, in the world and also in my own body. Menakem is a Black author, and a trauma therapist; but he writes with both clarity and compassion for three distinct audiences in this book - Black Americans, White Americans, and American Police (of whatever ethnicity).<br/><br/>I took a while to read the book; he's very emphatic about stopping and taking time to engage in a series of practices he provides. I just w</span>
  <span id="freeText4717580172048387657" style="display:none">This is a wonderful book. It gave me a rich new way to understand and think about how racism operates, in the world and also in my own body. Menakem is a Black author, and a trauma therapist; but he writes with both clarity and compassion for three distinct audiences in this book - Black Americans, White Americans, and American Police (of whatever ethnicity).<br /><br />I took a while to read the book; he's very emphatic about stopping and taking time to engage in a series of practices he provides. I just wanted to read the ideas, so I skipped the first practice at first - but then I was busted: "If you’ve already skipped the previous activity, <i>stop</i>. Go back and complete it before reading further." A little challenging for my frame of mind, but I was glad that I followed the practices; in addition to their own benefits, they supplied a necessary context for understanding his work.<br /><br />One particular reframe that was useful to me as a white man was a new understanding of fragility in whites. I'm familiar with the concept of "white fragility" as it applies to race itself - the brittleness that we can bring to discussions, how easily we can collapse in shame or raise shields in defensiveness, which basically blocks the racial conversation. But he points out here that just as there is a myth of black resilience, based on the American legacy of using black people for brutal labor in brutal conditions; there's a corresponding myth of white fragility, of a lack of resilience - a tendency for White Americans to believe that they can't handle pain, they can't do things that are hard. I see what a disservice this has been to my own life. I see this in my fellow white men - in the culture - we resist Manning Up, so to speak, we want to remain immature. And that's bad for the world, but also profoundly unsatisfying for our own lives.<br /><br />In some cases, we tend to look to Black Americans to do the hard things for us. Including leading us out of racism - like in me, I'm frustrated with racism, and I'm looking for someone like a new Martin Luther King to tell me what to do about it. But <b>racism is primarily a White problem</b>, and it's up to us to lead ourselves out of it. (While certainly listening to Black voices and criticism, but creating our own new culture around race.)<br /><br />Menakem makes clear in particular that he and other Black Americans cannot lead us White folks to the new culture we need - but what he can do, and expresses very clearly in this work, is point out what <i>hasn't</i> been working.<br /><br /><blockquote>White Americans have not yet created any form of anti-white-supremacy culture. White Americans who seek to undo white-body supremacy have organizations; they have ideas and strategies and goals; they have initiatives; and they have energy, conviction, and hope. But they have little sense of community—and no culture to build and support such community. This needs to change. White allies must build culture, because culture trumps almost everything else.</blockquote><br /><br />I don't give 5 stars often. This is one of the most important books I've read this century. Wholehearted recommendation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4717580172048387657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14645754728422314919">“In today’s America, we tend to think of healing as something binary: either we’re broken or we’re healed from that brokenness. But that’s not how healing operates, and it’s almost never how human growth works. More often, healing and growth take place on a continuum, with innumerable points between utter brokenness and total health.”<br/><br/>Must read book.</span>

<div id="review_3446983730" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3446983730" />
    <a title="Eli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2023786-eli"><img alt="Eli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566751060p2/2023786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3446983730?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eli" href="/user/show/2023786-eli">Eli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3446983730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11806933094251783247">I'm real tempted to justify my whole two-star review by simply reporting that the author advocates police officers taking bubble baths as a significant part of the solution to police brutality.<br/><br/>But there's more to talk about. So here's the long version.<br/><br/>I wanted so badly to like this. The premise of this book is really deeply compelling. Unfortunately the author doesn't elaborate much on his initial ideas, beyond compiling other people's work and not explaining it very well. He indicates concepts </span>
  <span id="freeText11806933094251783247" style="display:none">I'm real tempted to justify my whole two-star review by simply reporting that the author advocates police officers taking bubble baths as a significant part of the solution to police brutality.<br /><br />But there's more to talk about. So here's the long version.<br /><br />I wanted so badly to like this. The premise of this book is really deeply compelling. Unfortunately the author doesn't elaborate much on his initial ideas, beyond compiling other people's work and not explaining it very well. He indicates concepts instead of teaching them. If you haven't explored white fragility or moral injury or somatic healing in other contexts, this might break some ground for you and be valuable for that reason. But all subjects brought up here have deeper and more competent treatments available elsewhere. And the parts here touching on police violence are just an absolute wreck.<br /><br />The body awareness exercises here include: <br />- entirely intellect-oriented exercises with "and how does your body feel?" added on at the end, which isn't actual body work; <br />- unexpected and untagged visualizations of stressful or traumatic situations, which is a poor decision for a book that purports to work respectfully with trauma;<br />- and some rudimentary, superficial body practices around trauma, vaguely explained and often "supported" by inaccurate neurological explanations. <br /><br />The depth of the embodiment work here is a disappointment, rarely exploring further than insights like 'antiracist leaders should find a signature garment to wear to inspire solidarity'.<br /><br />Phrases like soul nerve, and clean pain vs dirty pain, are introduced as vital concepts but only clumsily and superficially handled. Also included is generalized diet and weight loss advice, which is inappropriate for anyone serious about bodywork.<br /><br />As mentioned above, his analysis of police violence is... woefully inadequate. He does give lip service to the violent history of the system. But he is then overwhelmingly focused on what roles job stress and unintended blunders play in cops killing Black folks, insisting that cops being relaxed enough (he mentions essential oils as well as massage) will impact this juggernaut system stacked against Black folks. The chapter on police body healing involves solutions ranging from cosmetic to invasive in nature, as though cops showing up at Black churches on Sunday morning will fix the carceral state. There's a lack of consistency -- in one chapter, he specifies that police have in fact become an occupying force in Black communities; in another chapter, he shames civilians who see them as that occupying force. It's important that the reader know that the author makes his living in part by training police departments in "self-care" practices - including the Minnneapolis PD where he lives - and he has law enforcement in his immediate family (both of which he is upfront about). This no doubt impacts his working assumptions that policing has fallen away from noble roots it never had, and that the central problem embedded bodily in the system now is just that the job of policing is too stressful.<br /><br />This is a book that vaguely points toward a lot of good ideas. Just saying that bodies CAN heal from racial violence is indeed powerful and important. We need more somatic work done on racialized trauma. But we need it to be actual body work, not mislabelled cognitive self-reflection, and not a hodge-podge of basic relaxation and simple body-scanning techniques. And we need this work to come out of a context that takes police brutality seriously, that doesn't minimize it or advocate police rescuing more cats from trees as a band-aid for it (and yes, that is another actual suggestion from the book).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11806933094251783247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3268256608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3268256608" />
    <a title="Haven Wright" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25280055-haven-wright"><img alt="Haven Wright" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997044p2/25280055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3268256608?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haven Wright" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haven Wright" href="/user/show/25280055-haven-wright">Haven Wright</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25280055-haven-wright?shelf=siue-reading-list">siue-reading-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3268256608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15680910987360728483">For some reason it doesn’t feel right to rate this book. It was a self-help book I didn’t know I needed. The premise is how trauma doesn’t live just in our minds but also in our bodies. Along with historical and psychological information there are activities for practice to help settle your body as the author calls it. <br/><br/>One in particular really got to me. It required you to think of your ancestry (something I don’t know a lot about the further out it gets) and the trauma they faced. I ended up ma</span>
  <span id="freeText15680910987360728483" style="display:none">For some reason it doesn’t feel right to rate this book. It was a self-help book I didn’t know I needed. The premise is how trauma doesn’t live just in our minds but also in our bodies. Along with historical and psychological information there are activities for practice to help settle your body as the author calls it. <br /><br />One in particular really got to me. It required you to think of your ancestry (something I don’t know a lot about the further out it gets) and the trauma they faced. I ended up making a tree tracking as far back as I could remember and calling my family to ask them about life experiences that were especially hard or formative. What I ended up finding was our own personal brand of trauma that within three generations I found repetition. This was hard. It gave me a different perspective on pain. I hurt for my family who had gone through very hard events and I also felt a new kind of solidarity. That I wasn’t alone. I’m not just an outcome. I’m a point in a process of genetic resilience. It’s interesting to think of my anxiety, for example, as a generational genetic alteration in our DNA rather than MY singular disability. <br /><br />I also thought the history of violence that has been perpetrated by white people was especially interesting. The book talked a lot about the medieval punishments we inflicted on ourselves which pushed some of us to flee Europe, later the gruesome events involved in slavery, and even our more modern and normalized forms such as whupping children. I don’t want to cause harm to people and I do my best to not. However, back to my anxiety, it causes me a very persistent drive to chew on my bottom lip. So maybe violence has just manifested itself differently in my body. I don’t want to hurt myself either. This was just something I was thinking about. <br /><br />Anyways, there’s also parts broken down into white Americans, African Americans, and police officers and the different types of trauma that lives in each body. I thought there were great ways the author mentioned in order to heal and overcome these things so that we (white people and police officers) can stop causing one another harm. <br /><br />One thing I’ve learned recently is that racism exists on a spectrum just like many other things and even if you don’t use hate speech or actively treat people differently there are passive ways it occurs too within our body language. There were also activities in the book to help you determine if you display any of them and how to ease those bodily tensions. <br /><br />Overall, I think this book’s message is that in order to heal we can’t just address the mental without the psychical as well because you may not feel any superiority to minorities but your body may subconsciously feel more nervous around them and that’s what leads police officers to feel like their life is threatened in situations that it is not and thus use much riskier and deadly tactics. It’s up to us to learn these things about ourselves so that we stop causing harm.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15680910987360728483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176973087" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Berger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51356747-jeffrey-berger"><img alt="Jeffrey Berger" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176973087?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Berger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Berger" href="/user/show/51356747-jeffrey-berger">Jeffrey Berger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176973087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1967255102377223604">This ground-breaking book begins with a warning:<br/><blockquote><br/> <p><b>If the persistence of white supremacy in America surprises you,</b> this book will give you a startlingly different understanding of why ... </p><br/> <p><b>If you are not surprised that widespread white supremacy continues to injure America, but have little hope for overcoming it,</b> keep reading ... </p><br/> <p><b>If you see white supremacy as a belief system or ideology,</b> in this book you will discover only a fraction of it exists in our cognitive brains ... </p><br/> <p><b>If you are convinced </b></p></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1967255102377223604" style="display:none">This ground-breaking book begins with a warning:<br /><blockquote><br /> <p><b>If the persistence of white supremacy in America surprises you,</b> this book will give you a startlingly different understanding of why ... </p><br /> <p><b>If you are not surprised that widespread white supremacy continues to injure America, but have little hope for overcoming it,</b> keep reading ... </p><br /> <p><b>If you see white supremacy as a belief system or ideology,</b> in this book you will discover only a fraction of it exists in our cognitive brains ... </p><br /> <p><b>If you are convinced that ending white supremacy begins with social and political action,</b><i> do not read this book unless you are willing to be challenged ...</i></p><br /> <p><b>If you believe America's racial tensions lie not in white supremacy but in its dark-skinned people and the power they wield,</b><i> do not read further.</i> The pages ahead will trigger your trauma reflexes and make your life more painful than it already is.</p><br /></blockquote><br /><p>As one who thinks that white supremacy is intimately connected with the grievous crises we face -- extreme inequality in wealth, the growing danger of fascism, the threat of world war, our civilization-ending climate crisis -- I found this book essential to understanding how best to respond to them.</p><br /><p>Read it.</p></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313952653" />
    <a title="Lauren Siegel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32225224-lauren-siegel"><img alt="Lauren Siegel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525268145p2/32225224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313952653?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Siegel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Siegel" href="/user/show/32225224-lauren-siegel">Lauren Siegel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313952653" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7068640474426062137">I happened to read "White Fragility" before reading this book and that was really the best thing to do (for myself at least). Resmaa references White Fragility in his book quite a bit and it gets at racism the from first some cognitive/"things to know" and then Resmaa's book takes into a "body practice" how to feel out racialized trauma and work through it. I would seriously recommend this book for anyone. It has practical things you can do to identify and work through your own racialized trauma</span>
  <span id="freeText7068640474426062137" style="display:none">I happened to read "White Fragility" before reading this book and that was really the best thing to do (for myself at least). Resmaa references White Fragility in his book quite a bit and it gets at racism the from first some cognitive/"things to know" and then Resmaa's book takes into a "body practice" how to feel out racialized trauma and work through it. I would seriously recommend this book for anyone. It has practical things you can do to identify and work through your own racialized trauma. He also is so good at framing concepts I already knew in a different way so that I understand them better. One example is why white guilt is so harmful. i listened to this as an audiobook, which was also a good choice. </span>

<div id="review_2632849814" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2632849814" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Schroeder" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1199673-elizabeth-schroeder"><img alt="Elizabeth Schroeder" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569203847p2/1199673.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2632849814?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Schroeder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Schroeder" href="/user/show/1199673-elizabeth-schroeder">Elizabeth Schroeder</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199673-elizabeth-schroeder?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199673-elizabeth-schroeder?shelf=racial-justice">racial-justice</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2632849814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8972824473812425969">I like reviews that have pull-out quotes from the book folks have just finished. With this book, I flagged so many quotes, I would've almost been transcribing chapters at a time -- so I'll just share my review!<br/><br/>This powerful book is part educational experience, part healing journey. It is written by a Black cis-male therapist, Resmaa Menakem, who has expertise in helping people heal from trauma. The main focus is that the trauma caused by racism goes back generations and lives in our bodies; ther</span>
  <span id="freeText8972824473812425969" style="display:none">I like reviews that have pull-out quotes from the book folks have just finished. With this book, I flagged so many quotes, I would've almost been transcribing chapters at a time -- so I'll just share my review!<br /><br />This powerful book is part educational experience, part healing journey. It is written by a Black cis-male therapist, Resmaa Menakem, who has expertise in helping people heal from trauma. The main focus is that the trauma caused by racism goes back generations and lives in our bodies; therefore, the only way forward toward healing is to deal with that trauma. (This is a REALLY watered-down summary; he is/does much more than this, and the book is about much more as well).<br /><br />Mr. Menakem specifically addresses people with three types of bodies in this book: Black bodies, white bodies, and police bodies (independent of other characteristics/skin color). Even though he specifies when he is talking to any one of these groups of people, he encourages all readers to read all chapters. This, to me, was an invaluable part of the process of this book.<br /><br />He also includes some activities that I strongly urge anyone who reads this book to do. As a white person, I struggled at first with the concept of how racism would live in my white body, as I have not suffered from it. What became so clear to me, however, is that the trauma of the history of white bodies perpetuating the harshest, most inhumane forms of racism absolutely lives in our bodies -- as does the ways in which our present-day commissions of micro aggressions and reinforcement of white supremacy, and the trauma that our presence as white-bodied people can cause BIPOC just by existing. If we as white-bodied people want to show up more completely and effectively as allies and in proactively working to be anti-racist and pro-equality, we have our own healing to do.<br /><br />This book does not center whiteness; far from it. My review is speaking to the impact of the book on me as a white-bodied person because that is one of my identities and realities. Everyone's experience will be unique to them. For that and so many other reasons, I strongly recommend this book no matter your body or your experiences living in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8972824473812425969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer3275923707184439966">Shoutout to the Show Up cohort for holding space for this immensely valuable read. Adding to the syllabus!<br/><br/>Menakem offers a different approach to antiracism through the lens of trauma psychology, breaking down “hero-villain” dichotomies and teaching practical self-soothing tools to help us settle into our bodies. Racism, he argues, is first and foremost an embodied experience—felt and perpetuated primarily in the physical world rather than the abstract. By addressing racial oppressions in this wa</span>
  <span id="freeText3275923707184439966" style="display:none">Shoutout to the Show Up cohort for holding space for this immensely valuable read. Adding to the syllabus!<br /><br />Menakem offers a different approach to antiracism through the lens of trauma psychology, breaking down “hero-villain” dichotomies and teaching practical self-soothing tools to help us settle into our bodies. Racism, he argues, is first and foremost an embodied experience—felt and perpetuated primarily in the physical world rather than the abstract. By addressing racial oppressions in this way, Menakem empowers readers to discern when our bodies are activated and settled, and to understand how to guide ourselves between those two states without doing further harm to ourselves or others. <br /><br />I am going to revisit this again. Super powerful. This book and its exercises helped me to become more aware of my body as it operates in and responds to a racialized script. Go off-script, Maggie!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36167466-my-grandmother-s-hands">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3393959518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4430785164401142195"><strong>Powerful and helpful </strong><br/><br/>This is a great book. I have not found any other book that adressesthe issue of race and white body supremacy, not from a cognitive perspective, but through the body. Trauma therapists know that you can't just think your way out of amygdala responses. You have to become attuned to your body in real time. This book is compassionate and non judgemental, yet it challenges people to take responsibility for their emotions and reactions- like adult. I'm so glad I found this gem. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5711829570516340036">Great beginning book for the layperson who is just starting to explore racialized trauma and how to take steps to create change and become aware of their white privilege. Great somatic and thought provoking exercises throughout the book. <br/><br/>I did feel like the book could of been shorter; chapters could of been added together and condensed, that he repeated himself a lot.<br/><br/>As a therapist myself I was hoping for a bit more in depth exploration of what this would look like in session with clients, with </span>
  <span id="freeText5711829570516340036" style="display:none">Great beginning book for the layperson who is just starting to explore racialized trauma and how to take steps to create change and become aware of their white privilege. Great somatic and thought provoking exercises throughout the book. <br /><br />I did feel like the book could of been shorter; chapters could of been added together and condensed, that he repeated himself a lot.<br /><br />As a therapist myself I was hoping for a bit more in depth exploration of what this would look like in session with clients, with case studies of his work. Maybe the next book! :)</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+fRtqo8ZYjWs0ucGFF+YfRwmO9McZvz/0KqbIAhPijBgIrT1NMi4g/LHfFUNqnxaz9ndvea5kjBW6DIgcWKM0g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
